F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:83:We subsequently explored the potential of GO-SS-AA-C12 pLNP to promote T cell activation and limit T cell exhaustion via an in vitro serial culture assay (Supplementary Figs. 60-63). In brief, MC38 cells were treated with PBS (negative control) or GO-SS-AA-C12 pLNP encapsulating either IL-12 mRNA or FLuc mRNA. After 24 h, the supernatant of each group was collected and used to culture primary mouse CD3<sup>+</sup>T cells. Following 48 h of culture, T cells were collected and analysed for production of key effector cytokines, including tumour necrosis factor-α  $(TNF-\alpha)$ , interferon-y (IFNy) and granzyme B (Supplementary Fig. 60a). Cytokine levels were measured via intracellular cytokine staining and flow cytometry. CD3<sup>+</sup> T cells cultured in supernatant from MC38 cells treated with GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP exhibited notably higher levels of TNF- $\alpha$ , IFNy and granzyme B compared with those cultured in control supernatants (Supplementary Fig. 60). Moreover, treatment with GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP enhanced cytokine production in CD4<sup>+</sup> and CD8<sup>+</sup> T cells (Supplementary Figs. 61 and 62) and enhanced T cell proliferation (Supplementary Fig. 67).
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:85:The capacity of GO-SS-AA-C12 pLNP to mitigate T cell exhaustion was evaluated by co-culturing primary OT-I CD3<sup>+</sup> T cells with ovalbumin-modified MC38 (MC38-OVA) cancer cells at a 1:1 effector-to-target (E:T) ratio. GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP and GO-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP were added at 0.5 µg per well for 3 days. Cells treated with PBS served as a negative control. Every 3 days, equivalent numbers of MC38-OVA cells and corresponding amounts of mRNApLNP were added, for a total of 5 cycles, to mimic chronic T cell stimulation within the TME. After the final stimulation, cells were collected and analysed via flow cytometry for CD69 and CD25 expression, markers of T cell activation, and for PD-1 expression, a marker of T cell exhaustion<sup>5,46</sup> (Fig. 3h). Treatment with GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP upregulated CD69 and CD25 on OT-I CD3+T cells (Fig. 3i,j and Supplementary Figs. 64a,b and 65) and downregulated PD-1 (Fig. 3k and Supplementary Figs. 64c and 66) relative to control groups. Interestingly, GO-SS-AA-C12 pLNP encapsulating IL-12 mRNA mediated greater suppression of PD-1 expression than pLNP encapsulating FLuc mRNA (Fig. 3k and Supplementary Fig. 64c). Together, these results imply a synergistic mechanism between the released indoximod and translated IL-12 in resisting T cell exhaustion.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:87:# pLNP delivering IL-12 mRNA enables MC38 tumour immunotherapy
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:89:We next evaluated the therapeutic efficacy of GO-SS-AA-C12 pLNP in an MC38 tumour mouse model. To highlight the synergistic effect of this platform, composed of both a small-molecule IDO inhibitor and therapeutic IL-12 mRNA, we prepared two control LNPs. GO-SS-AA-C12 pLNP encapsulating FLuc mRNA was used to assess the effect of IDO inhibitor only, while GO-6C-AA-C12 LNP encapsulating IL-12 mRNA was used to evaluate the anti-tumour efficacy of IL-12 mRNA only (Supplementary Fig. 68). After subcutaneous injection of MC38 cells into the right flank of mice, GO-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP, GO-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP or GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP were administered intratumourally at an mRNA dose of 2.5 µg per mouse on days 6, 8 and 10 (Fig. 4a). PBS was administered via the same procedure as a negative control. GO-SS-AA-C12 pLNP encapsulating IL-12 mRNA suppressed tumour
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:91:<span id="page-6-0"></span>**Fig. 5** | **Characterization of TME after treatment with GO-SS-AA IL-12 pLNPs encapsulating IL-12 mRNA. a**, Schematic showing establishment of the MC38 tumour model for flow cytometry and bulk RNA sequencing (RNA-seq) after treatment. Mice bearing MC38 tumours received intratumoural injection of PBS, GO-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP, GO-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP or GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP. On day 12, tumours in each treatment group were collected, and a portion of tumour tissues was digested into a single-cell suspension for analysis of T cell populations via flow cytometry, while the remaining cells were digested for RNA-seq of tumour tissues. **b,c**, Quantification of CD8\* T cells (**b**) and CD4\* T cells (**c**) among CD3\* T cells in tumour tissues after different treatments (n = 5). **d,e**, Analysis of PD-1 expression on the surface of CD8\* T cells (**d**) and CD4\* T cells (**e**) (n = 5). **f,g**, Cytokine levels of TNF-α (**f**) and IFNy (**g**) in tumour tissues (n = 3).
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:93:growth (Fig. 4b), inducing compelete tumour regression in all treated mice within 31 days of model initiation (Fig. 4b,c). In comparison, G0-SS-AA-C12 pLNP encapsulating FLuc mRNA and G0-6C-AA-C12 LNP encapsulating IL-12 mRNA only partially inhibited tumour growth (Fig. 4b,c). All LNPs were well tolerated with no effect on body weight (Fig. 4d) or major organ histology (Supplementary Fig. 69) relative to control mice. Finally, PBS-treated mice succumbed to tumour burden before day 45, G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP and G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP treatment moderately increased survival, and all G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP-treated mice survived to our study endpoint (Fig. 4e).
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:95:To further characterize the importance of co-formulation of the IDO inhibitor with IL-12 mRNA in a single LNP, we evaluated three additional control groups: free IL-12 mRNA, free IDO inhibitor and G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP with free IDO inhibitor (Supplementary Fig. 70a). GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP demonstrated superior anti-tumour efficacy compared to these control groups. Neither free IL-12 mRNA nor free IDO inhibitor alone notably suppressed tumour growth (Supplementary Fig. 70b,e). G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP plus free IDO inhibitor only partially inhibited tumour progression with mean tumour volumes rising rapidly after day 22 (Supplementary Fig. 70b,c). By contrast, GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP completely suppressed tumour growth, and achieved complete regression of all tumours within 32 days in this study (Supplementary Fig. 70c,e). All mice in the GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP-treated group survived to study endpoint (Supplementary Fig. 70d). Splenic CD4+, CD8+ and regulatory T cell response was also assessed for each of these groups on day 12 (Supplementary Fig. 71a). Notably, GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP elicited a robust CD8<sup>+</sup>T cell response and diminished the number of CD4<sup>+</sup> and regulatory T cells compared with control groups (Supplementary Figs. 71-73). Overall, these data confirmed that co-formulation of both an IDO inhibitor and IL-12 mRNA in a single LNP is integral to induction of a potent immune response and anti-tumour efficacy.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:97:We next investigated the anti-tumour mechanism of G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP. Given that IL-12 is known to activate cells in both the innate and adaptive immune compartment and the spleen plays a major role in immunoregulation  $^{47,48}$ , we more specifically explored the effect of pLNPs specifically on splenic T cell populations in the MC38 tumour mouse model. As observed previously, G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP biased splenic T cells towards CD8 $^{+}$  populations and away from CD4 $^{+}$  populations relative to control groups (Fig. 4f–h). More specifically, G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP enhanced effector memory (CD44 $^{+}$ CD62L $^{-}$ ) and central memory (CD44 $^{+}$ CD62L $^{+}$ ) CD4 $^{+}$  and CD8 $^{+}$  splenic T cell populations (Fig. 4i–l and Supplementary Figs. 74 and 75), and reduced the presence of splenic regulatory T cells (CD4 $^{+}$ CD25 $^{+}$ FOXP3 $^{+}$ ) (Fig. 4m and Supplementary Figs. 76 and 77). Together, these results demonstrate that G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP achieves anti-tumour efficacy via immune priming towards an effector T cell phenotype while also generating long-term immune memory.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:99:# pLNP drives effector T cell infiltration and TME activation
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:101:Having characterized the impact of GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP on splenic immunoregulation, we next evaluated the mechanisms of anti-tumour efficacy in MC38 tumours. A subcutaneous MC38 tumour mouse model
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:103:**h**, Volcano plots of changes in gene expression ( $\log_2$ ) between MC38 tumours treated with PBS and GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNPs. i, IFN $\gamma$  gene expression after treatment with GO-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP and GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP relative to PBS treatment (n=3). **j-o**, Heat maps of differentially expressed genes, including pro-inflammatory cytokines (**j**), leukocyte chemokines (**k**), T cell priming and DC activation (**l**), NOD-like receptor signalling pathway (**m**), apoptosis (**n**) and T cell and natural killer cell activation (**o**), in response to treatment with PBS or GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP. Data are presented as mean  $\pm$  s.d. (n=3). Statistical differences were calculated using one-way ANOVA with Tukey's multiple comparisons test. Statistical difference in **i** was calculated using t-tests. \*\*\*\*P < 0.001; \*\*\*P < 0.001; \*\*\*P < 0.01; \*\*P < 0.05. Panel **a** created in BioRender; Hamilton, A. https://biorender.com/1kx9cw2 (2025).
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:105:was prepared and treated with either PBS, GO-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP, GO-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP or GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP as described previously. On day 12, tumours were collected and digested into single-cell suspensions (Fig. 5a). GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP increased CD8<sup>+</sup> T cells
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:111:in T cell infiltration, intracellular levels of TNF-α, IFNγ and granzyme B in CD3<sup>+</sup> T cells were elevated after treatment with G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP (Supplementary Fig. 78a,b,d–i). Relative to PBS-treated tumours, G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP downregulated PD-1 expression on CD4+ and CD8<sup>+</sup> T cells, demonstrating the influence of the released IDO inhibitor (Fig. [5d,e\)](#page-6-0). G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP further decreased CD4<sup>+</sup> and CD8<sup>+</sup> T cell exhaustion in the TME, demonstrating further synergy in therapeutic function between IL-12 and IDO inhibitor (Fig. [5d,e](#page-6-0) and Supplementary Figs. 81 and 82). G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP also significantly elevated pro-inflammatory cytokines IL-6, TNF-α and IFNγ levels in tumour tissues (Fig. [5f,g](#page-6-0) and Supplementary Fig. 78a–c). Finally, G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP maintained performance relative to tumours treated with free IL-12 mRNA, free IDO inhibitor and G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP with free IDO inhibitor (Supplementary Figs. 79 and 80), highlighting the importance of IDO inhibitor and IL-12 mRNA co-formulation. Thus, G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP enhances effector T cell infiltration and reduces T cell exhaustion in the TME via synergistic mechanisms, leading to the anti-tumour efficacy observed in the MC38 tumour mouse model.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:113:To understand the impact of IDO inhibitor and IL-12 release from pLNPs on the gene expression profile of cells within the TME, we performed bulk RNA sequencing (RNA-seq) on collected MC38 tumours (Fig. [5a,h–o](#page-6-0)). IL-12 exerts many of its downstream effects via IFN[γ49.](#page-11-27) Thus, it was unsurprising that both G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP- and G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP-treated tumours had an upregulation of IFNγ transcripts by 6.3-fold and 2.1-fold, respectively, relative to PBS-treated tumours (Fig. [5i](#page-6-0)), which was consistent with high IFNγ levels in tumour tissue (Fig. [5g\)](#page-6-0). Twenty-eight pro-inflammatory cytokine genes were significantly enriched following treatment with G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP (Fig. [5j](#page-6-0) and Supplementary Fig. 83a), while G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP and G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP induced expression of 11 and 4 genes, respectively (Supplementary Figs. 84 and 85). At a macro level, G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP shifted the gene expression profile of the TME from 'cold' to 'hot', evidenced by upregulation of leukocyte chemokines and pathways responsible for T cell priming, dendritic cell (DC) activation, nucleotide-binding oligomerization domain (NOD)-like receptor signalling, cancer cell apoptosis, and T cell and natural killer (NK) cell activation (Fig. [5j–o](#page-6-0)). By contrast, G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP and G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP induced only modest changes in immune-response genes (Supplementary Figs. 83b,c, 84 and 85). These data imply that G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNPs modulate the TME by exerting immunostimulatory effects that lead to the anti-tumour efficacy of this platform.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:115:#### **Anti-tumour efficacy and safety of pLNP after systemic dosing**
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:117:Given the robust anti-tumour efficacy of G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP after intratumoural administration, we further explored the efficacy of pLNP after intravenous administration in a mouse MC38 tumour model. Mice were treated with free IL-12 mRNA, free IDO inhibitor, G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP, G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP, G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:119:<span id="page-8-0"></span>**Fig. 6 | Intratumoural injection of G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP elicits effective long-term anti-tumour response and drives regression of distal tumours. a**, Schematic depicting in vivo MC38 tumour rechallenge. Mice bearing ~100 mm<sup>3</sup> MC38 tumours were injected with G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP on days 6, 8 and 10, resulting in tumour elimination by day 30. Then, MC38 cells were subcutaneously reinjected into the same position to monitor tumour regrowth and mouse survival. Mice naive to pLNP treatment served as a control group. **b**, Mean tumour volume from two independent experiments. **c**, Spider plots of individual tumour growth curves of each mouse in the treatment group and control group. **d**, Survival curve of mice for the treatment group compared with the control group. **e**, Body weight changes of mice in the treatment group and control group. The biologically independent samples in **b**–**d** were *n* = 5 for the control group and *n* = 8 for the treated group. **f**, Scheme depicting the bilateral tumour model. Mice were treated with PBS, G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP, G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:121:LNP plus free IDO inhibitor, or G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP at an mRNA dose of 2.5 μg per mouse on days 6, 8 and 10 (Supplementary Fig. 86a). Treatment with PBS served as a negative control. Treatment with G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP, G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP or G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP with free IDO inhibitor inhibited tumour growth (Supplementary Fig. 86b). In comparison, free IL-12 mRNA and free IDO inhibitor failed to exhibit anti-tumour function relative to the PBS-treated group (Supplementary Fig. 86c). Long-term monitoring of tumour progression and mouse survival showed that while LNPs encapsulating IL-12 mRNA partially suppressed tumour burden, they were unable to eradicate tumours (Supplementary Fig. 86d).
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:123:We next assessed systemic toxicity of the seven distinct treatment groups. Serum was collected on day 12 for assessment of cytokine levels, liver function markers and pro-inflammatory cytokines (Supplementary Fig. 87a). All LNPs encapsulating IL-12 mRNA elevated serum levels of IL-6, TNF-α and IFNγ after intravenous injection (Supplementary Fig. 87b–d), while treatment with free IL-12 mRNA, free IDO inhibitor and G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc LNP resulted in serum cytokine levels comparable to the negative control (Supplementary Fig. 87b–d). Similarly, all LNPs encapsulating IL-12 mRNA increased levels of the liver enzymes aspartate aminotransferase (AST) and alanine aminotransferase (ALT) compared with the PBS group (Supplementary Fig. 88). By contrast, G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP administered via intratumoural injection did not increase serum IL-6 and TNF-α relative to PBS treatment (Supplementary Fig. 87e–g), and these cytokine levels were 3.4-fold and 2.2-fold lower, respectively, than those after intravenous administration of pLNP (Supplementary Fig. 87h,i). No significant hepatotoxicity was observed after intratumoural injection of any treatment (Supplementary Fig. 89). Together, although pLNP encapsulating IL-12 mRNA has moderate anti-tumour efficacy after intravenous injection, systemic toxicity limits the potential of the platform via systemic administration. By contrast, intratumoural injection of pLNP encapsulating IL-12 mRNA boasts significant anti-cancer efficacy with minimal systemic toxicity.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:125:#### **Intratumoural pLNP administration prevents rechallenge and regresses distal tumours**
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:127:Since G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNPs elicited a substantial memory T cell response upon intratumoural administration, we tested whether this platform could be used to protect against tumour rechallenge. To this end, we inoculated mice with subcutaneous MC38 tumours and administered G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP intratumourally at an mRNA dose of 2.5 μg per mouse on days 6, 8 and 10. On day 30, MC38 cancer cells were injected into the flank of mice with primary MC38 tumours that were previously eliminated by pLNP treatment or age-matched normal mice as a control (Fig. [6a](#page-8-0)). All mice that successfully eliminated their primary tumours after G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP treatment rejected growth of a secondary tumour (Fig. [6b,c](#page-8-0)) and survived to the terminal endpoint (>60 days) without detectable tumour burden (Fig. [6d\)](#page-8-0). By contrast, control mice grew tumours (Fig. [6b,c](#page-8-0)) and all succumbed to their tumour burden within 40 days (Fig. [6d](#page-8-0)). No loss in body weight
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:129:or G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP in only the right tumour. Tumour growth and mouse survival in each group were monitored. **g**, Representative images of tumours on day 30 after initiation of treatment. **h**, Spider plots of individual tumour growth curves of each mouse in different treatment groups. **i**, Survival curves from the four different treatment groups. **j**, Body weight changes of mice in the treatment group and control group. The biologically independent samples in **h**–**j** were *n* = 5 for PBS and G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP groups, *n* = 4 for G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP and G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP groups. **k**,**l**, Quantification of CD8<sup>+</sup> T cells (**k**) and CD4+ T cells (**l**) among CD3<sup>+</sup> T cells in contralateral tumour tissue after treatment (*n* = 3). Data are presented as mean ± s.d. Statistical differences in **b** were calculated using two-way ANOVA with Sidak's multiple comparisons test. Survival analysis in **d** was performed using a log-rank (Mantel–Cox) test. \*\*\*\**P* < 0.0001; \*\*\**P* < 0.001; \*\**P* < 0.01; \**P* < 0.05.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:133:was observed in the treatment group after tumour rechallenge (Fig. [6e\)](#page-8-0). Taken together, G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP not only has the potential to treat and eliminate primary tumours, but can also induce sufficient immune memory to protect against local tumour regrowth.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:135:We next probed whether the global immunomodulatory effect of G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP could drive the regression of tumours distal to the primary tumour injection site. To test this, mice were inoculated with two subcutaneous MC38 tumours, one on each flank. Then, only the right tumour was injected with either PBS (negative control), G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP, G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP or G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP at an mRNA dose of 2.5 μg per mouse on days 6, 8 and 10 (Fig. [6f\)](#page-8-0). G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP induced notable regression of not only the treated tumour but also the contralateral tumour (Fig. [6g,h\)](#page-8-0). All mice treated with G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP survived to the terminal endpoint, nearly 3 months after tumour inoculation (Fig. [6i\)](#page-8-0). By contrast, both flank tumours of G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP-treated mice showed rapid growth and resulted in minimal survival benefit relative to PBS-treated mice, demonstrating that IDO inhibitor alone is not sufficient for therapeutic efficacy (Fig. [6h,i](#page-8-0)). For the G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP-treated mice, untreated distal tumour growth was not inhibited (Fig. [6h](#page-8-0)), limiting long-term survival without a cleavable IDO inhibitor (Fig. [6i\)](#page-8-0). No body weight changes were observed in all treatment groups, demonstrating the biocompatibility of pLNP platforms (Fig. [6j\)](#page-8-0). Finally, we explored changes in T cell populations within the contralateral TME via flow cytometry. Akin to the perturbation of T cell populations observed within the primary tumour (Fig. [5b](#page-6-0)), treatment with G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP resulted in greater CD8+ T cells in the contralateral tumour relative to control groups (Fig. [6k,l](#page-8-0) and Supplementary Fig. 90). Of note, G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP resulted in lower numbers of CD4+ T cells in the contralateral tumour relative to control groups (Fig. [6k,l](#page-8-0) and Supplementary Fig. 90), likely resulting in effective tumour regression owing to reduction of tumour-protective regulatory T cells. Together, these results imply that both IDO inhibitor release and IL-12 expression are necessary within pLNP for elimination of distal tumours and maximal therapeutic efficacy of this platform.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:139:In this study, we engineered a synergistic immunotherapy platform, G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP, which showed robust anti-tumour efficacy. Further optimization of this therapeutic platform could be accomplished by balancing pLNP stability and IDO inhibitor release. Several factors influence pLNP stability, including the tail length of pIL and the molar ratio of the helper lipids in the LN[P50,](#page-11-28) which modulate the intramolecular forces that drive pLNP formulation. The chemical structures of constituent lipids within pLNPs are likely to influence IDO release kinetics. Different linker chemistries may be designed to respond to specific biological triggers in the TME, such as pH, redox markers (for example, reactive oxygen species (ROS) and GSH) or enzymatic activity[41](#page-11-20). While in the present study we utilized a cyclic reaction for IDO inhibitor release, self-immolative linkers based on 1,6- or 1,4-azaquinone methide elimination could also be used to precisely control IDO inhibitor release kinetics[51](#page-11-29). Optimization of these parameters may identify a next-generation pLNP formulation that balances stability and IDO inhibitor release to achieve superior therapeutic outcomes.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:141:Intravenous administration of G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNPs demonstrated significant anti-tumour efficacy (Supplementary Fig. 86) but was accompanied by systemic toxicity, including cytokine release syndrome and hepatotoxicity in mice (Supplementary Figs. 87 and 88). To mitigate these adverse effects, several strategies could be implemented. For example, incorporating microRNA-122 target sequences (miR-122T) into the 3′-untranslated region of IL-12 mRNA may substantially reduce hepatic IL-12 expressio[n52](#page-11-30). Alternatively, the use of pro-IL-12 mRNA could generate an inactive precursor that is specifically activated within the TME. Conjugating a tumour-targeting antibody to pLNPs may further enhance tumour localization while minimizing hepatic transfection. Finally, co-administration of inhibitors targeting IL-6, TNF-α or IFNγ could reduce IL-12-induced toxicity without compromising anti-tumour efficacy.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:143:Although systemically administered immunotherapies (that is, checkpoint blockade, bispecific antibodies and adoptive T cell transfer) have had clinical success[53](#page-11-31), especially in haematologic cancer[s54,](#page-12-0) the majority of solid tumours have remained refractory to these therapies. For these difficult-to-treat cancers, intratumoural immunotherapies, a strategy that involves directly injecting immunostimulatory agents into tumour sites, are currently being tested in clinical trial[s55–](#page-12-1)[57](#page-12-2). Advantages of this approach include overcoming barriers of drug biodistribution to tumours and the ability to achieve high local concentrations of drug with lower systemic exposure. Indeed, while we observed systemic toxicity after intravenous administration of pLNPs encapsulating IL-12 mRNA (Supplementary Figs. 86 and 87), intratumoural administration of this platform elicited potent anti-cancer activity with a strong safety profile (Supplementary Fig. 87).
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:145:A critical requirement for the success of intratumoural immunotherapy is treating metastatic tumours via generation of a systemic anti-tumour immune response, referred to as the abscopal effect. This requires the intratumoural agent to trigger events leading to 'in situ' vaccination[58,](#page-12-3) that is, the generation or expansion of tumour-specific T cells that not only attack the tumour at the site of injection but also circulate and target distant, non-injected tumours. Encouragingly, in the present study, we observed that intratumoural injection of G0-SS-AA-C12 pLNP encapsulating IL-12 mRNA resulted in systemic (splenic) T cell activation (Fig. [4](#page-5-0)), immunologic memory (Figs. [4i–l](#page-5-0) and [6a–e\)](#page-8-0) and, importantly, a strong abscopal effect (Fig. [6f–j](#page-8-0)). These data support the use of pLNPs for disseminated cancers after local intratumoural injection.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:147:In summary, our data demonstrate the potential of G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP for solid tumour treatment and provide a framework to develop next-generation mRNA-LNP therapeutics, co-delivering both a small-molecule drug and an mRNA transcript, for cancer immunotherapy.

F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:230:DLin-MC3-DMA was obtained from MedChemExpress. 1,2-Dioleoyl-snglycero-3-phosphoethanolamine (DOPE), 1,2-distearoyl-sn-glycero-3-p hosphocholine (DSPC), cholesterol and 1,2-dimyristoyl-rac-glycero-3-m ethoxypolyethylene glycol-2000 (DMG-PEG 2000) were purchased from Avanti Polar Lipids. 2,2′-Disulfanediylbis(ethan-1-ol), 1-methyl-D-tryptophan, hexane-1,6-diol, 2-hydroxyethyl disulfide and polyamine heads were purchased from Sigma-Aldrich. Epoxydecane (C10), epoxydodecane (C12), epoxytetradecane (C14) and 4-nitrophenyl carbonochloridate were purchased from Tokyo Chemical Industry. All organic solvents were purchased from Fisher Scientific. FLuc mRNA (5moU) (L-7202) was purchased from TriLink BioTechnologies.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:232:#### **Preparation of LNPs**
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:234:For the preparation of MC3 LNPs, DLin-MC3-DMA, DSPC, cholesterol and DMG-PEG were mixed at a molar ratio of 50:10:38.5:1.5 and dissolved in 200 proof ethanol. For the preparation of other LNPs, ionizable lipid, DOPE, cholesterol and DMG-PEG were mixed at a molar ratio of 50:10:38.5:1.5 and dissolved in ethanol. mRNA was dissolved in 10 mM citrate buffer (pH = 3). For in vitro screening experiments, the ethanol phase and the citrate buffer phase were mixed using pipette mixing. For other in vitro experiments and animal experiments, the ethanol phase and the citrate buffer phase were mixed in a microfluidic chip device at a flow rate ratio of 1:3. LNPs were then purified by dialysing against 1× PBS (dialysis cassette molecular weight cut-off (MWCO) 20 kDa) for 2 h to remove ethanol and citrate buffer. A 0.22 μM pore size filtration device was used to remove any aggregates, and the LNPs were then stored at 4 °C until use. A Quant-iT RiboGreen RNA assay was used to quantify the mRNA encapsulation efficiency. mRNA encoding FLuc was used to formulate the LNPs for in vivo screening experiments.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:236:#### **In vitro screening of pLNPs**
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:238:HepG2 cells were seeded in 96-well plates at a density of 5,000 per well in 100 μl cell culture medium (DMEM, 10% FBS and 1% penicillin-streptomycin (P/S)) overnight. Then fresh DMEM medium was changed and pLNPs were added in the wells at a dose of 50 ng FLuc per well (MC3 LNPs served as a control). The expression of FLuc mRNA and cell viability were measured after treating cells for 24 h using a Luciferase Reporter 1000 Assay System (#E4550, Promega), and cell viability was measured using a CellTiter-Glo Luminescent Cell Viability Assay (#G7572, Promega) according to the manufacturer's protocols.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:240:#### **In vivo screening of pLNPs**
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:242:Female mice were intravenously injected with FLuc mRNA-loaded pLNPs at a dose of 2.5 μg per mouse (MC3 LNPs served as a positive control). D-Luciferin potassium salt (150 mg kg−1) was intraperitoneally injected into mice 6 h post-injection, and bioluminescence imaging was performed using an in vivo imaging system (PerkinElmer). For in vivo screening in a mouse tumour model, pLNPs encapsulating FLuc mRNA were intratumourally injected at a dose of 2.5 μg per mouse. After 6 h, mice were intraperitoneally injected with D-luciferin potassium salt (150 mg kg−1). After that, FLuc mRNA expression was measured by bioluminescence imaging using an in vivo imaging system (IVIS; PerkinElmer).
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:248:#### **Measuring pKa of mRNA-LNP**
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:250:TNS reagent was dissolved in ultrapure water at a concentration of 0.16 mM. Then, buffered solutions of 150 mM sodium chloride, 20 mM sodium phosphate, 25 mM ammonium citrate and 20 mM ammonium acetate were created and adjusted to different pH values ranging from 2.5 to 9.5 in increments of 0.5. After that, 2.5 μl of the LNP formulation was added to each pH-adjusted buffer solution in a black-wall black-bottom 96-well plate (3 wells for each pH). 6-(p-toluidino)-2-naphthalenesulfonic acid (TNS) reagent was then added to each well so that the final TNS concentration was 6 μM. The 96-well plate was incubated in a dark location for 5 min. Fluorescence at an excitation/emission of 322 nm/431 nm was measured using a fluorescence plate reader. The data were fitted to a sigmoidal curve, and the pKa was calculated as the pH corresponding to half of the maximum TNS fluorescence value.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:252:#### **Labelling LNPs with 3,3'-dioctadecyloxacarbocyanine perchlorate (DiO)**
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:254:One millilitre of LNPs was added to a 1.5 ml tube with 2 μl DMSO containing DiO (1 mg ml−1). After vortex mixing and incubation at room temperature (25 min), the mixture was loaded into a centrifugal filter device (MWCO 10 kDa) and LNP-DiO was washed with PBS three times to remove free DiO. The purified LNP-DiO nanoparticles were stored at 4 °C fridge before use.

F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:262:MC38 cells were seeded in confocal imaging dishes at a density of 5 × 10<sup>4</sup> cells per dish in 300 μl DMEM overnight. Afterwards, cells were washed with PBS 3 times and 300 μl PBS was added for following confocal imaging.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:266:MC38 cells were seeded in a 6-well plate at a cell density of 3 × 105 in 1.5 ml of DMEM overnight. F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:268:#### **In vitro IDO inhibitor indoximod (1-methyl-D-tryptophan) release from G0-SS-AA-C12 pLNP**
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:270:G0-SS-AA-C12 pLNP with the concentration of pIL at 1.7 mg ml−1 were dispersed in 100 μl PBS buffer containing 5 mM GSH. Then 50 μl external PBS buffer solution was used for high-performance liquid chromatography analysis at a detected wavelength of 286 nm at different time points. F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:272:#### **G0-SS-AA-C12 pLNP-mediated increase of T cell cytokine (TNF-α, IFNγ and granzyme B) secretion in vitro**
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:274:MC38 cells were incubated with either G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP or G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP at an mRNA dose of 0.5 μg ml−1 per well for 24 h, after which the culture supernatants were collected. Primary mouse CD3+ T cells were isolated from the spleens of female C57BL/6 mice using a CD3+ T cell isolation kit (catalogue number 480024, BioLegend) and subsequently activated with mouse T cell activation beads (catalogue number 11456D, Thermo Fisher) in complete T cell culture medium lacking mouse IL-2 (mIL-2) for 3 days. After removal of the activation beads, the CD3+ T cells were resuspended in medium. Supernatants from the treated MC38 cells were then mixed with T cell culture medium (without mIL-2) at a volume ratio of 1:1 and used to culture CD3+ T cells for 48 h (PBS served as a negative control). Following this incubation, T cells were collected and stimulated with a cell stimulation cocktail (catalogue number 00-4970- 93, Thermo Fisher) and a protein transport inhibitor cocktail (catalogue number 00-4930-93, Thermo Fisher) for 4 h. After stimulation, the cells were collected and stained for surface markers on ice for 1 h. They were then washed with PBS buffer and treated with fixation and permeabilization buffers, respectively. Intracellular cytokines were then stained with corresponding antibodies. Finally, cells were subjected to flow cytometry to assess intracellular TNF-α, IFNγ and granzyme B production.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:276:#### **G0-SS-AA-C12 pLNP-mediated T cell proliferation in vitro**
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:278:MC38 cells were treated with G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP and G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP for 24 h at a dose of 0.5 μg ml−1 per well, respectively. Then, supernatants were collected and mixed with T cell culture medium at a volume ratio of 1:1. Primary CD3+ T cells were isolated from the spleens of female C57BL/6 mice and activated by T cell activation beads for 3 days. After removal of all activation beads, T cells were dyed with a CFSE cell proliferation kit (catalogue number [C34554,](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/C34554) Thermo Fisher) and further cultured with T cell culture medium (without mIL-2) for 3 days. After that, CD3+ T cells were collected and subjected to flow cytometry to analyse T cell proliferation.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:280:#### **G0-SS-AA-C12 pLNP-mediated suppression of T cell exhaustion in vitro**
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:282:To investigate the effects of G0-SS-AA-C12 pLNP on T cell exhaustion, MC38-OVA cancer cells were co-cultured with primary OT-I CD3<sup>+</sup> T cells isolated from the spleens of OT-I female mice using a CD3<sup>+</sup> T cell isolation kit (catalogue number 480024, BioLegend). The cells were plated at an E:T ratio of 1:1 in a 6-well plate (MC38-OVA, 5 × 105 cells; OT-I CD3<sup>+</sup> T cells, 5 × 105 cells). G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP or G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP was then added to the co-culture system at an mRNA dose of 0.5 μg ml−1 per well, followed by incubation for 3 days. Subsequently, an additional 5 × 105 MC38-OVA cancer cells were added to the well along with a second dose of pLNP at the same mRNA dose (0.5 μg ml−1), and the culture was maintained for another 3 days. This process was repeated four times in total. At the end of the experiment, all cells were collected and analysed by flow cytometry to assess T cell activation, as indicated by CD69 and CD25 expression, and to evaluate changes in PD-1 levels, a key marker of T cell exhaustion.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:284:#### **Intratumoural administration of LNPs to evaluate the effect of cancer immunotherapy**
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:286:C57BL/6 mice (6–8 weeks) were subcutaneously inoculated ~1 × 106 MC38 cells on day 0. The treatments were performed in tumour-bearing mice at the indicated time points (days 6, 8 and 10) by intratumoural injection of G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP, G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP and G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP at a dose of 2.5 μg mRNA per mouse, respectively. Control mice were injected intratumourally with 50 μl of PBS. Tumours were then measured by a precision caliper with a 2,000 mm3 ethical limit, which was never exceeded in this study. Mice were also monitored for predefined humane endpoints, including tumour ulceration, and were euthanized and the last tumour measurement was recorded. At the same time, the body weights of mice were recorded. Complete tumour regression was defined as no measurable tumour by caliper and the tumour becoming no-palpable. All protocols performed on animals in this study were approved by the Institutional Animal Care and Use Committee of the University of Pennsylvania (protocol # 806540).
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:290:MC38 tumour tissues were collected on day 12 after 3 intratumoural injections of G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP, G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP, G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP and PBS, respectively. After that, total RNA was extracted. Sequencing was performed in Novogene, and the differentially expressed genes were analysed using DEGSeq R package (1.20.0). The *P* values were adjusted using the Benjamini–Hochberg method. The threshold of corrected *P* value of 0.05 and log2 (fold change) of 1 was selected to determine the significantly differentially expressed genes.

MC38 cells were used for in vitro screening of pLNPs encapsulating FLuc mRNA. F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:51:with indoximod (1-methyl-D-tryptophan) to obtain 4-Nitro-SS-AA (Supplementary Fig. 5). The presence of a disulfide linkage in this structure enables intracellular release of indoximod via GSH cleavage. Next, Nitro-SS-AA was reacted with seven amine heads to generate seven prodrug polyamine heads, and all structures were confirmed by
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:53:NMR and electrospray ionization mass spectrometry (ESI-MS) spectra (Fig. [1a](#page-1-0) and Supplementary Figs. 2 and 6–19). These structures were then reacted with 1 of the 3 epoxide-terminated alkyl tails for 12 h at 70 °C to yield a library of 21 pILs (Supplementary Fig. 3), and all structures of pILs were confirmed by NMR and high resolution mass spectrometry (HRMS) spectra (Supplementary Figs. 20–39). In this study, pILs are denoted by a specific nomenclature: P2A to DAB refers to the seven amine head groups, SS refers to the presence of a disulfide linkage, AA refers to the presence of 1-methyl-D-tryptophan, and C10/ C12/C14 refers to the length of the alkyl tails in the ionizable lipid. For example, 'G0-SS-AA-C12' has a G0 amine head, a disulfide linkage, 1-methyl-D-tryptophan and C12 alkyl tails.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:55:Next, the pILs were combined with 1,2-dioleoyl-sn-glycero-3-p hosphoethanolamine (DOPE), 1,2-dimyristoyl-rac-glycero-3-m ethoxypolyethylene glycol-2000 (DMG-PEG) and cholesterol in ethanol and pipette-mixed with 1-methylpseudouridine (m1ψ)-modified firefly luciferase (FLuc) mRNA to formulate 21 pLNPs. The molar ratio of pIL/cholesterol/DOPE/DMG-PEG was kept constant at 50:38.5:10:1.5 (Fig. [2a](#page-2-0)). The pLNP library was screened in HepG2 cells, an immortalized human hepatocellular carcinoma cell line. Among the 21 pILs, G0-based pILs had the highest transfection efficiency in vitro among the 7 amine head groups (Supplementary Fig. 47). The top eight pILs were advanced for study of in vivo efficiency following intravenous administration of pLNPs encapsulating FLuc mRNA at a dose of 2.5 μg per mouse. All pLNPs primarily transfected the liver. G0-based pLNPs (G0-SS-AA-C10/ C12/C14) exhibited higher expression of reporter protein compared with other LNPs, including LNPs containing the ionizable lipid MC3, which is used in US Food and Drug Administration (FDA)-approved formulations (Supplementary Fig. 48).
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:57:Then, we verified that pILs could be used to transfect an additional cancer cell line. We repeated a similar workflow, this time using MC38 cells, a mouse colon adenocarcinoma cell line (Fig. [2a\)](#page-2-0). Treatment of MC38 cells in vitro with our library of pLNPs encapsulating FLuc mRNA showed that G0-SS-AA-C12 pLNP had the highest transfection efficiency (Fig. [2b\)](#page-2-0). All pLNPs exhibited low cytotoxicity in vitro (Supplementary Fig. 49). To emphasize the structural advantage of the pIL, we also designed a control lipid, termed G0-6C-AA-C12, that could not release drug by substituting the disulfide linkage with carbon–carbon linkage (Supplementary Figs. 40–46). Interestingly, G0-SS-AA-C12 pLNP facilitated 1.5-fold greater transfection of MC38 cells than LNPs formulated with a structural analogue that lacked the disulfide linkage (G0-6C-AA-C12) (Supplementary Fig. 50). Since G0-6C-AA-C12 has a carbon–carbon bond instead of a disulfide linkage, it is unable to release indoximod in the cytoplasm, implying that the prodrug itself within the pIL potentially aids in pLNP-mediated mRNA transfection.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:59:The top three pILs (G0-SS-AA-C10, G0-SS-AA-C12 and G0-SS-AA-C14) from our initial screens were advanced for further study. Given our interest in applying pLNPs for solid tumour therapy, we next assessed pIL efficiency relative to two control lipids (G0-6C-AA-C12 and MC3) after intratumoural injection into mouse MC38 tumours. In brief, LNPs encapsulating FLuc mRNA at a dose of 2.5 μg per mouse were administered to MC38 tumour-bearing mice, and luciferase expression was quantified 6 h post-injection using bioluminescence imaging (Fig. [2c](#page-2-0) and Supplementary Fig. 51). G0-SS-AA-C12 pLNP facilitated greater whole-body mRNA transfection compared with MC3 LNP (Supplementary Fig. 51). Ex vivo quantification of luminescence intensity specifically within MC38 tumours demonstrated that G0-SS-AA-C12 pLNP outperformed other pLNPs and MC3 LNP (Fig. [2c\)](#page-2-0). Moreover, G0-SS-AA-C12 pLNP induced low off-target transfection of the liver, while MC3 LNP induced substantially higher liver transfection (Supplementary Fig. 51). On the basis of these data, G0-SS-AA-C12 was selected as the lead pIL for further study.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:61:Purified G0-SS-AA-C12 or G0-6C-AA-C12 were combined with standard excipients and mixed with FLuc mRNA using a microfluidic device to generate pLNPs for physiochemical characterization. Transmission electron microscopy images showed uniform, multilamellar, complex spherical morphologies of both G0-SS-AA-C12 pLNP and G0-6C-AA-C12 LNP with hydrodynamic diameters of 43 nm and 78 nm, polydispersity index values of 0.12 and 0.26, and slightly positive surface charges (Supplementary Figs. 52 and 53). FLuc mRNA encapsulation efficiency (EE) of G0-SS-AA-C12 pLNP and G0-6C-AA-C12 LNP was determined to be 91.2% and 89.6%, respectively, and their pKa values were approximately 6.67 and 6.50, respectively (Supplementary Figs. 52–54). Next, we compared the cellular uptake of G0-SS-AA-C12 pLNP, G0-6C-AA-C12 LNP and MC3 LNP via 3,3′-dioctadecyloxacarbocyanine perchlorate (DiO) labelling. Confocal imaging showed greater intracellular uptake of G0-SS-AA-C12 pLNP relative to MC3 and G0-6C-AA-C12 LNPs in MC38 cells (Supplementary Fig. 55). Moreover, we assessed the endosomal escape of the lead pLNP. A higher percentage of G0-SS-AA-C12 pLNP achieved endosomal escape compared with MC3 LNP in MC38 cells (Fig. [2d](#page-2-0)), demonstrating a potential mechanism for enhanced efficiency for the lead delivery platform.

F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:83:We subsequently explored the potential of GO-SS-AA-C12 pLNP to promote T cell activation and limit T cell exhaustion via an in vitro serial culture assay (Supplementary Figs. 60-63). F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:85:The capacity of GO-SS-AA-C12 pLNP to mitigate T cell exhaustion was evaluated by co-culturing primary OT-I CD3<sup>+</sup> T cells with ovalbumin-modified MC38 (MC38-OVA) cancer cells at a 1:1 effector-to-target (E:T) ratio. GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP and GO-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP were added at 0.5 µg per well for 3 days. Cells treated with PBS served as a negative control. Every 3 days, equivalent numbers of MC38-OVA cells and corresponding amounts of mRNApLNP were added, for a total of 5 cycles, to mimic chronic T cell stimulation within the TME. After the final stimulation, cells were collected and analysed via flow cytometry for CD69 and CD25 expression, markers of T cell activation, and for PD-1 expression, a marker of T cell exhaustion<sup>5,46</sup> (Fig. 3h). Treatment with GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP upregulated CD69 and CD25 on OT-I CD3+T cells (Fig. 3i,j and Supplementary Figs. 64a,b and 65) and downregulated PD-1 (Fig. 3k and Supplementary Figs. 64c and 66) relative to control groups. Interestingly, GO-SS-AA-C12 pLNP encapsulating IL-12 mRNA mediated greater suppression of PD-1 expression than pLNP encapsulating FLuc mRNA (Fig. 3k and Supplementary Fig. 64c). Together, these results imply a synergistic mechanism between the released indoximod and translated IL-12 in resisting T cell exhaustion.

F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:93:growth (Fig. 4b), inducing compelete tumour regression in all treated mice within 31 days of model initiation (Fig. 4b,c). In comparison, G0-SS-AA-C12 pLNP encapsulating FLuc mRNA and G0-6C-AA-C12 LNP encapsulating IL-12 mRNA only partially inhibited tumour growth (Fig. 4b,c). All LNPs were well tolerated with no effect on body weight (Fig. 4d) or major organ histology (Supplementary Fig. 69) relative to control mice. Finally, PBS-treated mice succumbed to tumour burden before day 45, G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP and G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP treatment moderately increased survival, and all G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP-treated mice survived to our study endpoint (Fig. 4e).
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:95:To further characterize the importance of co-formulation of the IDO inhibitor with IL-12 mRNA in a single LNP, we evaluated three additional control groups: free IL-12 mRNA, free IDO inhibitor and G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP with free IDO inhibitor (Supplementary Fig. 70a). GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP demonstrated superior anti-tumour efficacy compared to these control groups. Neither free IL-12 mRNA nor free IDO inhibitor alone notably suppressed tumour growth (Supplementary Fig. 70b,e). G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP plus free IDO inhibitor only partially inhibited tumour progression with mean tumour volumes rising rapidly after day 22 (Supplementary Fig. 70b,c). By contrast, GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP completely suppressed tumour growth, and achieved complete regression of all tumours within 32 days in this study (Supplementary Fig. 70c,e). All mice in the GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP-treated group survived to study endpoint (Supplementary Fig. 70d). Splenic CD4+, CD8+ and regulatory T cell response was also assessed for each of these groups on day 12 (Supplementary Fig. 71a). Notably, GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP elicited a robust CD8<sup>+</sup>T cell response and diminished the number of CD4<sup>+</sup> and regulatory T cells compared with control groups (Supplementary Figs. 71-73). Overall, these data confirmed that co-formulation of both an IDO inhibitor and IL-12 mRNA in a single LNP is integral to induction of a potent immune response and anti-tumour efficacy.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:97:We next investigated the anti-tumour mechanism of G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP. Given that IL-12 is known to activate cells in both the innate and adaptive immune compartment and the spleen plays a major role in immunoregulation  $^{47,48}$ , we more specifically explored the effect of pLNPs specifically on splenic T cell populations in the MC38 tumour mouse model. As observed previously, G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP biased splenic T cells towards CD8 $^{+}$  populations and away from CD4 $^{+}$  populations relative to control groups (Fig. 4f–h). More specifically, G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP enhanced effector memory (CD44 $^{+}$ CD62L $^{-}$ ) and central memory (CD44 $^{+}$ CD62L $^{+}$ ) CD4 $^{+}$  and CD8 $^{+}$  splenic T cell populations (Fig. 4i–l and Supplementary Figs. 74 and 75), and reduced the presence of splenic regulatory T cells (CD4 $^{+}$ CD25 $^{+}$ FOXP3 $^{+}$ ) (Fig. 4m and Supplementary Figs. 76 and 77). Together, these results demonstrate that G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP achieves anti-tumour efficacy via immune priming towards an effector T cell phenotype while also generating long-term immune memory.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:105:was prepared and treated with either PBS, GO-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP, GO-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP or GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP as described previously. On day 12, tumours were collected and digested into single-cell suspensions (Fig. 5a). GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP increased CD8<sup>+</sup> T cells
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:107:within the TME (Fig. 5b) relative to control groups, likely owing to IL-12-mediated recruitment and stimulation of T cell effector functions. There was no significant difference between the number of CD4 $^+$  cells between treatment groups (Fig. 5c). In line with the observed increase
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:111:in T cell infiltration, intracellular levels of TNF-α, IFNγ and granzyme B in CD3<sup>+</sup> T cells were elevated after treatment with G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP (Supplementary Fig. 78a,b,d–i). Relative to PBS-treated tumours, G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP downregulated PD-1 expression on CD4+ and CD8<sup>+</sup> T cells, demonstrating the influence of the released IDO inhibitor (Fig. [5d,e\)](#page-6-0). G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP further decreased CD4<sup>+</sup> and CD8<sup>+</sup> T cell exhaustion in the TME, demonstrating further synergy in therapeutic function between IL-12 and IDO inhibitor (Fig. [5d,e](#page-6-0) and Supplementary Figs. 81 and 82). G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP also significantly elevated pro-inflammatory cytokines IL-6, TNF-α and IFNγ levels in tumour tissues (Fig. [5f,g](#page-6-0) and Supplementary Fig. 78a–c). Finally, G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP maintained performance relative to tumours treated with free IL-12 mRNA, free IDO inhibitor and G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP with free IDO inhibitor (Supplementary Figs. 79 and 80), highlighting the importance of IDO inhibitor and IL-12 mRNA co-formulation. Thus, G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP enhances effector T cell infiltration and reduces T cell exhaustion in the TME via synergistic mechanisms, leading to the anti-tumour efficacy observed in the MC38 tumour mouse model.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:119:<span id="page-8-0"></span>**Fig. 6 | Intratumoural injection of G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP elicits effective long-term anti-tumour response and drives regression of distal tumours. a**, Schematic depicting in vivo MC38 tumour rechallenge. Mice bearing ~100 mm<sup>3</sup> MC38 tumours were injected with G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP on days 6, 8 and 10, resulting in tumour elimination by day 30. Then, MC38 cells were subcutaneously reinjected into the same position to monitor tumour regrowth and mouse survival. Mice naive to pLNP treatment served as a control group. **b**, Mean tumour volume from two independent experiments. **c**, Spider plots of individual tumour growth curves of each mouse in the treatment group and control group. **d**, Survival curve of mice for the treatment group compared with the control group. **e**, Body weight changes of mice in the treatment group and control group. The biologically independent samples in **b**–**d** were *n* = 5 for the control group and *n* = 8 for the treated group. **f**, Scheme depicting the bilateral tumour model. Mice were treated with PBS, G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP, G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:123:We next assessed systemic toxicity of the seven distinct treatment groups. Serum was collected on day 12 for assessment of cytokine levels, liver function markers and pro-inflammatory cytokines (Supplementary Fig. 87a). All LNPs encapsulating IL-12 mRNA elevated serum levels of IL-6, TNF-α and IFNγ after intravenous injection (Supplementary Fig. 87b–d), while treatment with free IL-12 mRNA, free IDO inhibitor and G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc LNP resulted in serum cytokine levels comparable to the negative control (Supplementary Fig. 87b–d). Similarly, all LNPs encapsulating IL-12 mRNA increased levels of the liver enzymes aspartate aminotransferase (AST) and alanine aminotransferase (ALT) compared with the PBS group (Supplementary Fig. 88). By contrast, G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP administered via intratumoural injection did not increase serum IL-6 and TNF-α relative to PBS treatment (Supplementary Fig. 87e–g), and these cytokine levels were 3.4-fold and 2.2-fold lower, respectively, than those after intravenous administration of pLNP (Supplementary Fig. 87h,i). No significant hepatotoxicity was observed after intratumoural injection of any treatment (Supplementary Fig. 89). Together, although pLNP encapsulating IL-12 mRNA has moderate anti-tumour efficacy after intravenous injection, systemic toxicity limits the potential of the platform via systemic administration. By contrast, intratumoural injection of pLNP encapsulating IL-12 mRNA boasts significant anti-cancer efficacy with minimal systemic toxicity.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:143:Although systemically administered immunotherapies (that is, checkpoint blockade, bispecific antibodies and adoptive T cell transfer) have had clinical success[53](#page-11-31), especially in haematologic cancer[s54,](#page-12-0) the majority of solid tumours have remained refractory to these therapies. For these difficult-to-treat cancers, intratumoural immunotherapies, a strategy that involves directly injecting immunostimulatory agents into tumour sites, are currently being tested in clinical trial[s55–](#page-12-1)[57](#page-12-2). Advantages of this approach include overcoming barriers of drug biodistribution to tumours and the ability to achieve high local concentrations of drug with lower systemic exposure. Indeed, while we observed systemic toxicity after intravenous administration of pLNPs encapsulating IL-12 mRNA (Supplementary Figs. 86 and 87), intratumoural administration of this platform elicited potent anti-cancer activity with a strong safety profile (Supplementary Fig. 87).

F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\41565_2025_2102_MOESM1_ESM\41565_2025_2102_MOESM1_ESM.md:124:*Synthesis of Nitro-SS-Nitro*. 4-Nitrophenyl carbonochloridate (2.4 equiv.), triethylamine (3 equiv.) and 50 mL of THF were added into a reaction flask. Then 2-hydroxyethyl disulfide (1 equiv.) was dissolved in 50 mL THF and slowly added into the flask. The mixture was stirred at room temperature overnight. Upon completion, the reaction mixture was filtered to remove undissolved substance and collect filtrates. After removing all the solvents on a rotary evaporator, the residues were further purified using a CombiFlash Rf-200i on silica gel using hexane:ethyl acetate (v:v = 6:1) as eluent to afford Nitro-SS-Nitro (yield: 80%). 1H NMR (400 MHz, CDCl3, Supplementary Fig. 4): δ 8.30 (d, *J* = 9.2 Hz, 4H), 7.41 (d, *J* = 9.2 Hz, 4H), 4.59 (t, *J* = 6.5 Hz, 4H), 3.11 (t, *J* = 6.5 Hz, 4H).
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\41565_2025_2102_MOESM1_ESM\41565_2025_2102_MOESM1_ESM.md:126:*Synthesis of Nitro-SS-AA*. Nitro-SS-Nitro (1.2 equiv.) and triethylamine (1.5 equiv.) were dissolved in 20 mL THF in a reaction flask and stirred at 0 oC. Then 1-methyl-*D*-tryptophan (1 equiv.) was dissolved in a mixture of THF and NaHCO3 aqueous (v:v = 1:3) and slowly added into the reaction flask. The reaction mixture was allowed to warm to room temperature under stirring for 3 h. Upon completion, THF was removed under reduced pressure. The residues were poured into 100 mL ethyl acetate and washed with 50 mL saturated NaCl solution three times. The organic layer was collected and dried over anhydrous Na2SO4, filtered and evaporated to dryness under reduced pressure. The residues were further purified by silica gel column chromatography using hexane:ethyl acetate = 1:1 as eluent to afford Nitro-SS-AA (yield: 52%). 1H NMR (400 MHz, DMSO-*d*6, Supplementary Fig. 5A): δ 8.32 (d, *J* = 9.2 Hz, 2H), 7.59 – 7.47 (m, 4H), 7.36 (s, 1H), 7.17 – 7.10 (m, 2H), 7.07 – 6.97 (m, 1H), 4.47 (t, *J* = 6.1 Hz, 1H), 4.27 – 4.08 (m, 3H), 3.72 (s, 3H), 3.20 – 2.92 (m, 6H). ESI-MS (m/z, Supplementary Fig. 5B): Calcd for [M+Na]+: 586.1, found: 585.8; Calcd for [M+H]+: 564.1, found: 563.8.

F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\41565_2025_2102_MOESM1_ESM\41565_2025_2102_MOESM1_ESM.md:188:*Synthesis of Nitro-6C-Nitro*. 4-Nitrophenyl carbonochloridate (2.4 equiv.), triethylamine (3 equiv.) and 50 mL THF were added into a reaction flask. Then 1,6-hexanediol (1 equiv.) was dissolved in 50 mL THF and slowly added into the flask. The mixture was stirred at room temperature overnight. Upon completion, the reaction mixture was filtered to remove undissolved substance and collect filtrates. After removing all the solvents on a rotary evaporator, the residues were further purified by combiflash on silica gel using hexane:ethyl acetate (v:v = 6:1) as eluent to afford Nitro-6C-Nitro (yield: 72%). 1H NMR (400 MHz, CDCl3, Supplementary Fig. 41): δ 8.34 – 8.26 (m, 4H), 7.44 – 7.37 (m, 4H), 4.33 (d, *J* = 6.5 Hz, 4H), 1.83 (p, *J* = 6.7 Hz, 4H), 1.61 – 1.44 (m, 4H).
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\41565_2025_2102_MOESM1_ESM\41565_2025_2102_MOESM1_ESM.md:190:*Synthesis of Nitro-6C-AA*. Nitro-6C-Nitro (1.2 equiv.) and triethylamine (1.5 equiv.) were dissolved in 20 mL THF in a reaction flask and stirred at 0 oC. Then 1-methyl-*D*-tryptophan (1 equiv.) was dissolved in a mixture of THF and NaHCO3 aqueous (v:v = 1:3) and slowly added into the reaction flask. The reaction mixture was allowed to warm to room temperature under stirring for 3 h. Upon completion, THF was removed under reduced pressure. The residues were poured into 100 mL ethyl acetate and washed with 50 mL saturated NaCl solution three times. The organic layer was collected and dried over anhydrous Na2SO4, filtered and evaporated to dryness under reduced pressure. The residues were further purified by silica gel column chromatography using hexane:ethyl acetate = 1:1 as eluent to afford Nitro-6C-AA (yield: 48%). 1H NMR (400 MHz, DMSO-*d*6, Supplementary Fig. 42A) δ 8.31 (d, *J* = 9.1 Hz, 2H), 7.58 – 7.51 (m, 3H), 7.35 (dd, *J* = 14.5, 8.1 Hz, 2H), 7.16 – 7.08 (m, 2H), 7.01 (t, *J* = 7.4 Hz, 1H), 4.26 – 4.15 (m, 3H), 3.89 (q, *J* = 6.7 Hz, 2H), 3.72 (s, 3H), 3.13 (d, *J* = 4.7 Hz, 1H), 3.02 – 2.96 (m, 1H), 1.65 (d, *J* = 7.2 Hz, 2H), 1.52 (t, *J* = 6.8 Hz, 2H), 0.96 (q, *J* = 3.6 Hz, 4H). 13C NMR (101 MHz, DMSO-*d*6, Supplementary Fig. 42B) δ 175.55, 157.76, 155.79, 152.92, 144.91, 135.93, 129.14, 125.42, 123.51, 121.06, 118.85, 110.06, 67.70, 62.33, 56.86, 32.74, 28.28, 25.36. ESI-MS (m/z, Supplementary Fig. 43): Calcd for [M+Na]+: 550.2, found: 549.9; Calcd for [M+H]+: 528.2, found: 528.0.

G0 (3 equiv.), triethylamine (1.5 equiv.) and 10 mL THF were added into a reaction flask and stirred at 0 oC. Then 4-Nitro-6C-AA (1 equiv.) dissolved in THF was slowly added into the flask. After stirring for 2 h, all solvents were removed by reduced pressure. More broadly, pLNPs offer a generalizable strategy to engineer small-molecule-conjugated mRNA-LNP platforms for cancer immunotherapy.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:83:We subsequently explored the potential of GO-SS-AA-C12 pLNP to promote T cell activation and limit T cell exhaustion via an in vitro serial culture assay (Supplementary Figs. 60-63). In brief, MC38 cells were treated with PBS (negative control) or GO-SS-AA-C12 pLNP encapsulating either IL-12 mRNA or FLuc mRNA. After 24 h, the supernatant of each group was collected and used to culture primary mouse CD3<sup>+</sup>T cells. Following 48 h of culture, T cells were collected and analysed for production of key effector cytokines, including tumour necrosis factor-α  $(TNF-\alpha)$ , interferon-y (IFNy) and granzyme B (Supplementary Fig. 60a). Cytokine levels were measured via intracellular cytokine staining and flow cytometry. CD3<sup>+</sup> T cells cultured in supernatant from MC38 cells treated with GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP exhibited notably higher levels of TNF- $\alpha$ , IFNy and granzyme B compared with those cultured in control supernatants (Supplementary Fig. 60). Moreover, treatment with GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP enhanced cytokine production in CD4<sup>+</sup> and CD8<sup>+</sup> T cells (Supplementary Figs. 61 and 62) and enhanced T cell proliferation (Supplementary Fig. 67).
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:85:The capacity of GO-SS-AA-C12 pLNP to mitigate T cell exhaustion was evaluated by co-culturing primary OT-I CD3<sup>+</sup> T cells with ovalbumin-modified MC38 (MC38-OVA) cancer cells at a 1:1 effector-to-target (E:T) ratio. GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP and GO-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP were added at 0.5 µg per well for 3 days. Cells treated with PBS served as a negative control. Every 3 days, equivalent numbers of MC38-OVA cells and corresponding amounts of mRNApLNP were added, for a total of 5 cycles, to mimic chronic T cell stimulation within the TME. After the final stimulation, cells were collected and analysed via flow cytometry for CD69 and CD25 expression, markers of T cell activation, and for PD-1 expression, a marker of T cell exhaustion<sup>5,46</sup> (Fig. 3h). Treatment with GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP upregulated CD69 and CD25 on OT-I CD3+T cells (Fig. 3i,j and Supplementary Figs. 64a,b and 65) and downregulated PD-1 (Fig. 3k and Supplementary Figs. 64c and 66) relative to control groups. Interestingly, GO-SS-AA-C12 pLNP encapsulating IL-12 mRNA mediated greater suppression of PD-1 expression than pLNP encapsulating FLuc mRNA (Fig. 3k and Supplementary Fig. 64c). Together, these results imply a synergistic mechanism between the released indoximod and translated IL-12 in resisting T cell exhaustion.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:89:We next evaluated the therapeutic efficacy of GO-SS-AA-C12 pLNP in an MC38 tumour mouse model. To highlight the synergistic effect of this platform, composed of both a small-molecule IDO inhibitor and therapeutic IL-12 mRNA, we prepared two control LNPs. GO-SS-AA-C12 pLNP encapsulating FLuc mRNA was used to assess the effect of IDO inhibitor only, while GO-6C-AA-C12 LNP encapsulating IL-12 mRNA was used to evaluate the anti-tumour efficacy of IL-12 mRNA only (Supplementary Fig. 68). After subcutaneous injection of MC38 cells into the right flank of mice, GO-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP, GO-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP or GO-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP were administered intratumourally at an mRNA dose of 2.5 µg per mouse on days 6, 8 and 10 (Fig. 4a). PBS was administered via the same procedure as a negative control. GO-SS-AA-C12 pLNP encapsulating IL-12 mRNA suppressed tumour
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:93:growth (Fig. 4b), inducing compelete tumour regression in all treated mice within 31 days of model initiation (Fig. 4b,c). In comparison, G0-SS-AA-C12 pLNP encapsulating FLuc mRNA and G0-6C-AA-C12 LNP encapsulating IL-12 mRNA only partially inhibited tumour growth (Fig. 4b,c). All LNPs were well tolerated with no effect on body weight (Fig. 4d) or major organ histology (Supplementary Fig. 69) relative to control mice. Finally, PBS-treated mice succumbed to tumour burden before day 45, G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP and G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP treatment moderately increased survival, and all G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP-treated mice survived to our study endpoint (Fig. 4e).
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:119:<span id="page-8-0"></span>**Fig. 6 | Intratumoural injection of G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP elicits effective long-term anti-tumour response and drives regression of distal tumours. a**, Schematic depicting in vivo MC38 tumour rechallenge. Mice bearing ~100 mm<sup>3</sup> MC38 tumours were injected with G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP on days 6, 8 and 10, resulting in tumour elimination by day 30. Then, MC38 cells were subcutaneously reinjected into the same position to monitor tumour regrowth and mouse survival. Mice naive to pLNP treatment served as a control group. **b**, Mean tumour volume from two independent experiments. **c**, Spider plots of individual tumour growth curves of each mouse in the treatment group and control group. **d**, Survival curve of mice for the treatment group compared with the control group. **e**, Body weight changes of mice in the treatment group and control group. The biologically independent samples in **b**–**d** were *n* = 5 for the control group and *n* = 8 for the treated group. **f**, Scheme depicting the bilateral tumour model. Mice were treated with PBS, G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP, G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:125:#### **Intratumoural pLNP administration prevents rechallenge and regresses distal tumours**
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:127:Since G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNPs elicited a substantial memory T cell response upon intratumoural administration, we tested whether this platform could be used to protect against tumour rechallenge. To this end, we inoculated mice with subcutaneous MC38 tumours and administered G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP intratumourally at an mRNA dose of 2.5 μg per mouse on days 6, 8 and 10. On day 30, MC38 cancer cells were injected into the flank of mice with primary MC38 tumours that were previously eliminated by pLNP treatment or age-matched normal mice as a control (Fig. [6a](#page-8-0)). All mice that successfully eliminated their primary tumours after G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP treatment rejected growth of a secondary tumour (Fig. [6b,c](#page-8-0)) and survived to the terminal endpoint (>60 days) without detectable tumour burden (Fig. [6d\)](#page-8-0). By contrast, control mice grew tumours (Fig. [6b,c](#page-8-0)) and all succumbed to their tumour burden within 40 days (Fig. [6d](#page-8-0)). No loss in body weight
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:129:or G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP in only the right tumour. Tumour growth and mouse survival in each group were monitored. **g**, Representative images of tumours on day 30 after initiation of treatment. **h**, Spider plots of individual tumour growth curves of each mouse in different treatment groups. **i**, Survival curves from the four different treatment groups. **j**, Body weight changes of mice in the treatment group and control group. The biologically independent samples in **h**–**j** were *n* = 5 for PBS and G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP groups, *n* = 4 for G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP and G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP groups. **k**,**l**, Quantification of CD8<sup>+</sup> T cells (**k**) and CD4+ T cells (**l**) among CD3<sup>+</sup> T cells in contralateral tumour tissue after treatment (*n* = 3). Data are presented as mean ± s.d. Statistical differences in **b** were calculated using two-way ANOVA with Sidak's multiple comparisons test. Survival analysis in **d** was performed using a log-rank (Mantel–Cox) test. \*\*\*\**P* < 0.0001; \*\*\**P* < 0.001; \*\**P* < 0.01; \**P* < 0.05.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:133:was observed in the treatment group after tumour rechallenge (Fig. [6e\)](#page-8-0). Taken together, G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP not only has the potential to treat and eliminate primary tumours, but can also induce sufficient immune memory to protect against local tumour regrowth.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:135:We next probed whether the global immunomodulatory effect of G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP could drive the regression of tumours distal to the primary tumour injection site. To test this, mice were inoculated with two subcutaneous MC38 tumours, one on each flank. Then, only the right tumour was injected with either PBS (negative control), G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP, G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP or G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP at an mRNA dose of 2.5 μg per mouse on days 6, 8 and 10 (Fig. [6f\)](#page-8-0). G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP induced notable regression of not only the treated tumour but also the contralateral tumour (Fig. [6g,h\)](#page-8-0). All mice treated with G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP survived to the terminal endpoint, nearly 3 months after tumour inoculation (Fig. [6i\)](#page-8-0). By contrast, both flank tumours of G0-SS-AA-C12 FLuc pLNP-treated mice showed rapid growth and resulted in minimal survival benefit relative to PBS-treated mice, demonstrating that IDO inhibitor alone is not sufficient for therapeutic efficacy (Fig. [6h,i](#page-8-0)). For the G0-6C-AA-C12 IL-12 LNP-treated mice, untreated distal tumour growth was not inhibited (Fig. [6h](#page-8-0)), limiting long-term survival without a cleavable IDO inhibitor (Fig. [6i\)](#page-8-0). No body weight changes were observed in all treatment groups, demonstrating the biocompatibility of pLNP platforms (Fig. [6j\)](#page-8-0). Finally, we explored changes in T cell populations within the contralateral TME via flow cytometry. Akin to the perturbation of T cell populations observed within the primary tumour (Fig. [5b](#page-6-0)), treatment with G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP resulted in greater CD8+ T cells in the contralateral tumour relative to control groups (Fig. [6k,l](#page-8-0) and Supplementary Fig. 90). Of note, G0-SS-AA-C12 IL-12 pLNP resulted in lower numbers of CD4+ T cells in the contralateral tumour relative to control groups (Fig. [6k,l](#page-8-0) and Supplementary Fig. 90), likely resulting in effective tumour regression owing to reduction of tumour-protective regulatory T cells. Together, these results imply that both IDO inhibitor release and IL-12 expression are necessary within pLNP for elimination of distal tumours and maximal therapeutic efficacy of this platform.
F:\내 드라이브\EXTRACT-TEST\QS_2026_3\QS_2026\QS_2026.md:145:A critical requirement for the success of intratumoural immunotherapy is treating metastatic tumours via generation of a systemic anti-tumour immune response, referred to as the abscopal effect. This requires the intratumoural agent to trigger events leading to 'in situ' vaccination[58,](#page-12-3) that is, the generation or expansion of tumour-specific T cells that not only attack the tumour at the site of injection but also circulate and target distant, non-injected tumours. Encouragingly, in the present study, we observed that intratumoural injection of G0-SS-AA-C12 pLNP encapsulating IL-12 mRNA resulted in systemic (splenic) T cell activation (Fig. [4](#page-5-0)), immunologic memory (Figs. [4i–l](#page-5-0) and [6a–e\)](#page-8-0) and, importantly, a strong abscopal effect (Fig. [6f–j](#page-8-0)). These data support the use of pLNPs for disseminated cancers after local intratumoural injection.

def clean_label(x):
    if x is None or (isinstance(x,float) and math.isnan(x)): return ''
    s=str(x).strip()
    if s.lower() in ('nan','none'): return ''
    return s.replace('GO-','G0-').replace('GO_','G0_').replace('G0-6C-AA_C12','G0-6C-AA-C12')

def mapping_for(item):
    m=figmap.get(item.lower(),{}) or {}
    return {k:clean_label(m.get(k,'')) for k in ['source_image','source_pdf','source_page','selected_source_for_paneling']}

def excel_for(item, block_id=None):
    rows=excel_by_item.get(item.lower(),[])
    if block_id:
        rows=[r for r in rows if clean_label(r.get('block_id'))==block_id] or rows
    if not rows: return {}
    r=rows[0]
    return {k:clean_label(r.get(k,'')) for k in ['excel_file','excel_sheet','block_id','block_csv_path','evidence_excel']}

def base_row(item, visual_type, confidence='high'):
    m=mapping_for(item)
    r={c:'' for c in columns}
    r.update({'Paper_ID':paper_id,'Item_ID':item,'visual_type':visual_type,'source_type':source_doc.get(item.lower(),'')})
    r.update(m)
    r['Experiment_batching']='individual'
    r['confidence']=confidence
    r['manual_required']='false'
    return r

def apply_formulation(r, name):
    name=clean_label(name)
    r['Formulation_Name']=name
    if not name or name.upper()=='PBS':
        r['formulation_id']='QS_2026_CTRL_PBS' if name.upper()=='PBS' else ''
        return
    if 'free IL-12 mRNA' in name:
        r['formulation_id']='QS_2026_CTRL_FREE_IL12_mRNA'; r['Cargo']='mRNA'; r['Cargo_type']='IL-12'; return
    if 'free IDO' in name or 'IDO inhibitor' == name:
        r['formulation_id']='QS_2026_CTRL_FREE_IDO'; r['Fifth_component_name']='indoximod'; return
    # normalize labels without cargo suffix
    lipid=name
    for suffix in [' FLuc pLNP',' FLuc LNP',' IL-12 pLNP',' IL-12 LNP',' pLNP',' LNP']:
        lipid=lipid.replace(suffix,'')
    lipid=lipid.strip()
    if name=='MC3' or lipid=='MC3':
        r['formulation_id']='QS_2026_F_MC3'
        r['IL_name']='DLin-MC3-DMA'; r['HL_name']='DSPC'
    else:
        r['formulation_id']='QS_2026_F_'+re.sub(r'["'^A-Za-z0-9]+'"','_',lipid).strip('_')
        r['IL_name']=lipid; r['HL_name']='DOPE'
    r['IL_molarratio']='50'; r['HL_molarratio']='10'; r['CHL_name']='Cholesterol'; r['CHL_molarratio']='38.5'; r['PEG_name']='DMG-PEG2000'; r['PEG_molarratio']='1.5'
    if 'IL-12' in name: r['Cargo_type']='IL-12'
    elif 'FLuc' in name: r['Cargo_type']='FLuc'
    if r['Cargo_type']: r['Cargo']='mRNA'

def cond_invitro_screen(r, model='MC38', dose='0.05', method='luminescence', cargo_type='FLuc'):
    r.update({'Aqueous_buffer':'10 mM citrate buffer pH 3','Dialysis_buffer':'PBS','Mixing_method':'pipette','Model':'in_vitro','Model_type':model,'Model_target':'in_vitro','Route_of_administration':'in_vitro','Cargo':'mRNA','Cargo_type':cargo_type,'Dose_ug_nucleicacid':dose,'Experiment_method':method})

def cond_invitro_micro(r, model='MC38', method='ELISA_IL-12', cargo_type='IL-12'):
    r.update({'Aqueous_buffer':'10 mM citrate buffer pH 3','Dialysis_buffer':'PBS','Mixing_method':'microfluidic','Model':'in_vitro','Model_type':model,'Model_target':'in_vitro','Route_of_administration':'in_vitro','Cargo':'mRNA','Cargo_type':cargo_type,'Experiment_method':method})
    r['condition_1_name']='mRNA_concentration'; r['condition_1_value']='0.5 ug/mL'

def cond_invivomc38(r, target='tumor', method='IVIS'):
    r.update({'Aqueous_buffer':'10 mM citrate buffer pH 3','Dialysis_buffer':'PBS','Mixing_method':'microfluidic','Model':'in_vivo','Model_type':'Mouse_MC38_tumor','Model_target':target,'Route_of_administration':'intratumoral','Cargo':'mRNA','Dose_ug_nucleicacid':'2.5','Experiment_method':method})

def set_metric_from_values(r, metric, values, unit='', replicate_type='biological_replicate'):
    vals=[]
    for v in values:
        try:
            if pd.isna(v): continue
            fv=float(v)
            vals.append(fv)
        except Exception:
            pass
    if not vals: return
    r['metric_type']=metric
    r['original_values']='|'.join(f'{v:g}' for v in vals)
    r['aggregated_value']=f'{(sum(vals)/len(vals)):.10g}'
    r['unit']=unit
    r['replicate_type']=replicate_type
    extra=' Arithmetic mean computed from unambiguous replicate columns in mapped Excel block.'
    r['reason']=(r.get('reason','')+extra).strip()

def read_block(rel):
    return pd.read_csv(os.path.join(base,rel), header=None)

def group_values_from_block(rel):
    df=read_block(rel)
    # most bar/scatter blocks: row 0 is optional figure label, row 1 group labels, row 2 values; or row 0 labels row 1 values.
    if str(df.iloc[0,0]).startswith('Fig.'):
        labels=[clean_label(x) for x in df.iloc[1].tolist()]
        vals=df.iloc[2].tolist() if len(df)>2 else []
    else:
        labels=[clean_label(x) for x in df.iloc[0].tolist()]
        vals=df.iloc[1].tolist() if len(df)>1 else []
    out={}
    for lab,val in zip(labels,vals):
        if not lab or lab.startswith('Fig.'): continue
        out.setdefault(lab,[]).append(val)
    return out

def add_excel(r, item, erow=None):
    e=excel_for(item)
    if erow: e.update({k:clean_label(erow.get(k,'')) for k in ['excel_file','excel_sheet','block_id','block_csv_path','evidence_excel']})
    for k in ['excel_file','excel_sheet','block_id','block_csv_path']:
        r[k]=e.get(k,'')
    r['evidence_excel']=e.get('evidence_excel','')

rows=[]

def add_row(r):
    for c in smiles_cols: r[c]=''
    if r['manual_required'] in ('False','false',False): r['manual_required']='false'
    elif r['manual_required'] in ('True','true',True): r['manual_required']='true'
    rows.append({c:r.get(c,'') for c in columns})

# Figure 2B and Supplementary screening library rows
library_heads=['P2A-SS-AA','T3A-SS-AA','G0-SS-AA','110-SS-AA','306-SS-AA','L2A-SS-AA','DAB-SS-AA']
# derive actual rows from block for figure 2b
if 'figure 2b' in selected['item_id'].str.lower().values:
    item='figure 2b'; rel=excel_for(item).get('block_csv_path','')
    df=read_block(rel)
    for i in range(1,len(df)):
        head=clean_label(df.iloc[i,0])
        for tail,start in [('C10',1),('C12',4),('C14',7)]:
            name=f'{head}-{tail}'
            r=base_row(item,'heatmap')
            add_excel(r,item)
            cond_invitro_screen(r,'MC38','0.05','luminescence','FLuc')
            apply_formulation(r,name)
            r['evidence_text']=EVID['fig2']+' '+EVID['prep']
            r['evidence_image']=r['source_image']
            set_metric_from_values(r,'luminescence',df.iloc[i,start:start+3].tolist(),'RLU','biological_replicate')
            add_row(r)
